1. **$50,000 server** using the double-declining balance method.
2. **$200,000 AI cluster** using the sum-of-the-years'-digits method.
3. **$30,000 office furniture** using the straight-line method.

I'll proceed with the depreciation calculations. Let's work through those now. 

### Calculations

1. **Double-Declining Balance Method for Server**: 
   - Cost: $50,000
   - Salvage Value: $5,000
   - Useful Life: 5 years

   \[
   \text{Depreciation Rate} = \frac{2}{5} = 40\%
   \]

   - Year 1 Depreciation: \( 50,000 \times 0.4 = 20,000 \)
   - Book Value End of Year 1: \( 50,000 - 20,000 = 30,000 \)

   Continuing for the next years...

2. **Sum-of-the-Years'-Digits for AI Cluster**:
   - Cost: $200,000
   - Salvage Value: $0
   - Useful Life: 7 years

   Sum of the years: \( 1+2+3+4+5+6+7 = 28 \)

   - Year 1: \( \frac{7}{28} \times 200,000 \)
   - Continue for the rest...

3. **Straight-Line Method for Furniture**:
   - Cost: $30,000
   - Salvage Value: $3,000
   - Useful Life: 10 years

   \[
   \text{Annual Depreciation} = \frac{30,000 - 3,000}{10}
   \]

Let me perform the full calculations explicitly and summarize for Sarah.

Here’s a comprehensive tutorial covering the basics:\\n\\n1. **Quantum Bits (Qubits) and Superposition**: In classical computing, we use bits as the smallest unit of data, which can either be 0 or 1. In quantum computing, we have quantum bits or qubits. A qubit can exist in a state of 0, 1, or both at the same time, thanks to a property called superposition. A simple analogy is that while a light switch can either be off or on, a qubit can be both off and on at once until it is measured.\\n\\n2. **Quantum Gates and Circuits**: Quantum gates are the building blocks of quantum circuits, similar to how logic gates are used in classical circuits. They manipulate the states of qubits. For example, a Hadamard gate can put a qubit into a superposition state, effectively allowing the quantum computer to process multiple possibilities simultaneously.\\n\\n3. **Quantum Entanglement and Teleportation**: Entanglement is a unique phenomenon where two qubits become linked in such a way that the state of one directly affects the state of the other, no matter how far apart they are. For teleportation, it refers to the ability to transfer qubit states between particles without physically sending the particle itself, as if you could transmit information instantaneously!\\n\\n4. **Quantum Algorithms (Shor\'s, Grover\'s, etc.)**: An example is Shor\'s algorithm, which can factor large numbers exponentially faster than classical computers. Grover\'s algorithm can search unsorted databases much faster than traditional algorithms, demonstrating how quantum computing can provide significant speed advantages.\\n\\n5. **Potential Applications in Healthcare and Drug Discovery**: Quantum computing has potential applications such as simulating molecular interactions for drug discovery, leading to faster developments in pharmaceuticals that currently take much longer to discover using classical computing techniques.\\n\\n6. **Current Limitations and Challenges**: Despite its promise, quantum computing faces challenges, such as error rates in qubit calculations and the difficulty of maintaining superposition states long enough to perform meaningful computations.\\n\\nIf you would like more detailed explanations or specific examples for any of these concepts, let me know!\\n\\nBest,\\nFortuna"}', name='respond_to_email'), type='function')]

### Addressing Employee Requests

Next, I will focus on the unresolved requests from Sarah regarding her systematic futures strategy. Here’s how I can help her:

1. **Noisy Roll Yield Estimation**: If roll yields are noisy for less liquid contracts, consider adjusting your model to account for this by applying robust statistical techniques or filters that can smooth out noise.
  
2. **Basis Risk During Delivery Periods**: Address this by modeling the expected basis changes more dynamically or using historical performance to better inform current positions.
  
3. **Calendar Spread Arbitrage Execution**: Explore automation strategies that allow for faster execution of arbitrage opportunities. Algorithms that are attuned to market conditions may mitigate delays.
